  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

        state: 'apple_oauth_state_9cf3b838-cd3b-4a8c-9c23-c5632b84dc7a'
      });

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3408775440" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10983874830348754796">Adhaata Asao’s Liege is an interesting and enjoyable read set against a backdrop of Hinduism, and also other interesting influences. As a result, it creates a fascinating narrative. The story begins with the journey of five merchants, on their way home to ply their trade. I particularly enjoyed some of the vivid descriptions as they travelled through a country richly steeped in history, art, and culture. <br/>As the merchants’ journey on, the author steadily, and intriguingly leads the reader into an</span>
  <span id="freeText10983874830348754796" style="display:none">Adhaata Asao’s Liege is an interesting and enjoyable read set against a backdrop of Hinduism, and also other interesting influences. As a result, it creates a fascinating narrative. The story begins with the journey of five merchants, on their way home to ply their trade. I particularly enjoyed some of the vivid descriptions as they travelled through a country richly steeped in history, art, and culture. <br />As the merchants’ journey on, the author steadily, and intriguingly leads the reader into an increasingly mystical world of magical creatures. It is well worth checking out.<br /></span>

<div id="review_3345944741" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3345944741" />
    <a title="Sean" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/103673574-sean"><img alt="Sean" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3345944741?book_show_action=true">May 19, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sean" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sean" href="/user/show/103673574-sean">Sean</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3345944741" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11584866385767565367">Normally I enjoy books with a more medieval European or old Norse setting, but this Eastern inspired work is making me look into broadening my horizons. A great adventure with very well written characters leads you on a journey through a mystical world. Turning the standards of good and bad archetypes around with the portrayal of dwarves and dragons was a real treat. And as the narrative paints the world around you, the suspense keeps the pages turning.<br/>If, like me, you've only been looking into </span>
  <span id="freeText11584866385767565367" style="display:none">Normally I enjoy books with a more medieval European or old Norse setting, but this Eastern inspired work is making me look into broadening my horizons. A great adventure with very well written characters leads you on a journey through a mystical world. Turning the standards of good and bad archetypes around with the portrayal of dwarves and dragons was a real treat. And as the narrative paints the world around you, the suspense keeps the pages turning.<br />If, like me, you've only been looking into quasi-European fantasy stories then I highly recommend checking out Adhaata Asao's Liege to show you a new world of possibilities.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11584866385767565367" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3307483417" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3307483417" />
    <a title="Heidi Slowinski" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/102676838-heidi-slowinski"><img alt="Heidi Slowinski" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1568341508p2/102676838.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3307483417?book_show_action=true">May 02, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Heidi Slowinski" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Heidi Slowinski" href="/user/show/102676838-heidi-slowinski">Heidi Slowinski</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3307483417" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14586672451850480007">Lord Vishnu, protector of the world, is gathering Avatars to help humanity.<br/><br/>This is my first work by this author and I really enjoyed it. The language is wonderfully descriptive. I really liked the very vivid imagery. In a world with dragons, dwarfs, and avatars, I found parallels to Game of Thrones and Lord of the Rings. This fantasy was a wonderful escape!</span>

          </span>
        </div>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2155672463082615467">The story 'Adhaata Asao's Liege' starts with 5 merchants traveling on their way home from Purshapuam to ply their trade. To reach home, they have to cross the mountains to reach home, and they were far away from home. Rabhu, Gopall, Banku, Peru and their leader Aarnik were the 5 merchants. Rabhu and Gopall are the youngest in the group and are the best friends. They were in the middle of the desert and storm is dancing over their head, so to reach the nearest civilization they need to take a sho</span>
  <span id="freeText2155672463082615467" style="display:none">The story 'Adhaata Asao's Liege' starts with 5 merchants traveling on their way home from Purshapuam to ply their trade. To reach home, they have to cross the mountains to reach home, and they were far away from home. Rabhu, Gopall, Banku, Peru and their leader Aarnik were the 5 merchants. Rabhu and Gopall are the youngest in the group and are the best friends. They were in the middle of the desert and storm is dancing over their head, so to reach the nearest civilization they need to take a shortcut, a way faster than on the mountain. But it was said that the path was dangerous and cursed, a blood road and whoever crossed it never survived. Even though the path was dangerous, but their desperateness for rest that made others agree with the decision. But as said the 5 did lose someone in the valley, but who?<br /><br />A civilization Kushlam located between two mountains, a city of Lord Visnu, filled with gold and beautiful houses. A mahant (Monk) broke his 3 years austerity as he sensed the arrival of the destined one from the golden lake. Kushlam is Lord Visnu’s city and from thousands of years, the city had an enemy that only a few remember. Even though the city has forgotten the enemy, but the evil hasn’t and they still remember and are waiting for all these years to take revenge.<br /><br />The destined one is one of the 5 merchants and when the king, and others were told about his role, no one believes it, not even the destined one himself.<br /><br />But as said the destined one is the Avatar of Lord Vishnu and he will save the city of Kushlam from the evil army. How will he do that? Who is he?<br /><br />Also, the book contains dragons, a magical sword, beyond our imagination an epic storyline and divine power. <br /><br />My Take: <br /><br />I have read many mystic stories, but I found this the most uncomplicated book ever. Author Afroz Alam has written this book in a simple language and easy-to-understand storyline, that grasped my attention till the end. Who doesn’t loves dragons’? Well, I do and this is a perfect story for them, and again I’m just impressed by the writing style of the author and the storyline. All the characters were well defined and their roles were perfectly portrayed. The ending was also clever and perfectly timed. <br /><br />Overall, loved this book and if you are a dragon and adventure seeker, you must read this book and enjoy it just as I did. So read now the adventurous book of Adhaata Asao’s Liege by Afroz Alam:</span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5352022407295081862">It is a wonderful epic saga. It has many subplots and characters, but all are well designed, and well researched, like a full-grown Banyan tree, that has so many branches. This is the basic line. In a tale of adventure, fantasy, and warfare, a prophecy takes on an ancient enemy, that strives to destroy all of mankind. More than a thousand years ago, a dark enemy had been imprisoned in the caves of Mount Hemil, after the human community of Kushlam had come close to destruction. Trapped in the cav</span>
  <span id="freeText5352022407295081862" style="display:none">It is a wonderful epic saga. It has many subplots and characters, but all are well designed, and well researched, like a full-grown Banyan tree, that has so many branches. This is the basic line. In a tale of adventure, fantasy, and warfare, a prophecy takes on an ancient enemy, that strives to destroy all of mankind. More than a thousand years ago, a dark enemy had been imprisoned in the caves of Mount Hemil, after the human community of Kushlam had come close to destruction. Trapped in the caverns, the enemy waited for the right time to spring back into the world of the living and built their armies in secret. They were Hajud-Mhajud, the leaders of the dwarves. The tale comes to the present day when the prophecy has come close to its enactment. It has been told that only an incarnation of the Lord Vishnu would have the power to defeat and destroy the dark enemy of old. The incarnation’s business has remained until this day unfinished, and the prophecy draws Rabhu, a man unknown to his destiny, close to Kushlam as he and his four other companions journey under harsh weather on the passes of Mount Hemil. Rabhu falls down the dark deep valley, leaving his merchant companions, and is found unconscious on the edges of a golden pond, which is said to be impervious and protected by a golden shield. Surprise and curiosity take over the priests of Vishnu even as the present-day Mahant wakes up from his self-imposed Samadhi. As Mahant works towards healing Rabhu from the ordeals of his venture into the Golden Pond, he also convinces the King and his royal family of his intent to proclaim Rabhu as the Avatar “Adhaata” even with a distrustful Erbir, the commander-in-chief of Kushlam’s army, trying to prove Mahant false. Now that the Avatar had come, the enemy awakens in the mountains and send in the Ori army to lay siege to Kushlam. Only an incarnation of Lord Vishnu has the power to defeat and destroy the enemy of Kushlam. A farmer from Bamiyan, unaware of what destiny has in store for him, will he accept that he is the prophesized Avatar? Will he save Kushlam from its enemies and free the world from the fear of the trapped monsters who have found a way out of their infallible trap?</span>

  <span id="freeText3112274646958214955" style="display:none">I cannot tell you the experience of reading this book. This is my favorite novel of all times. I believe that Afroz's talent lies in character, relationship and world building and that's what makes books go from GOOD to GREAT to AWESOME. I really adore the characters in this book and Rabhu will always have a place in my heart. It is perfect mixture of Hebrew, Muslim (Gog Magog as Hajud Mhajud) and Hindu Mythology (Adhaata the Avatar of Lord Vishnu). I 100% recommend picking up this book. <br />I'm really glad I have read this book. Due to lockdown in this pandemic situation I had to choose kindle option but I will definitely add paperback in my library very soon and I will touch the magic of Afroz Alam through his book.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3112274646958214955" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText10627596702691995911" style="display:none">So being a lover of romance genre books, I rarely choose another genre to read. But today after reading this book, I realized how beautiful other genres book could be. <br /><br />Adhaata Asao's Liege, the title and cover and the reviews intrigued me to pick this book and let me tell you I loved the book. I loved the story and the way it is written. Everything about the book and story is great and can't be afforded to miss. <br /><br />There is a reason for the title, who is Adhaata, an incarnation of Lord Vishnu or a farmer? What is Asao? Mahant played an important role too.<br /> <br />Easy to read, Author's way of description, page-turner is what makes this book special. Recommended for those who are interested in short fictional mythology.</span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('0m9pwbOU3MM0tTSnp9bcZ1KZtZkv4rNFqKV6gPPRX5Ez2QSG+w5kLI2yU1A6bf8OQ53IBHshKgZlqfmBeNlMqA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('DmRdUpfpogU3d3QnbzixokfWk4wDovKzx2bxhheXg9fv0jAV33Ma6o5wE9Dyg5LLVtLuEVdha/AKanKHnJ+Q7g==')})
  }

She had married her beloved and her life was as perfect as she had ever imagined it to be. \n\nBut when tragedy strikes them yet again, their fundamentally fragile lives threaten to fall apart. \n\nCan Fiona and Soham overcome their grief? \n\nWill the overwhelming pain destroy their lives? \n\nSeasoned with the flavours of exotic Nepalese traditions and set in the picturesque Indian hill station, Gangtok, The Fragile Thread of Hope explores the themes of spirituality, faith, alcoholism, love and guilt while navigating the complex maze of family relationships. \n\nInspirational and heart-wrenchingly intimate, it urges you to wonder—does hope stand a chance in this travesty called life?\n\nReviews:\n\n“Well-sketched, sympathetic characters. He began his writing career with a book review blog and after several years of honing his writing skills, he wrote his debut solo novel The Fragile Thread of Hope. The inspirational fiction novel was selected as a “Top 5 Finalist” in the Amazon Pen to Publish Contest 2017 and received critical acclaim worldwide. It also led to him being felicitated by Sikkim Manipal University for his contribution to the literature of Sikkim and being invited by popular website YourStory.com and ABN TV, India’s first Nepali satellite channel, for exclusive interviews. \n\nHe is currently working in the government sector in Sikkim. He likes to kill time listening to progressive metal music and watching movies and sitcoms. <span id="freeTextContainer10195930897769430267">Afroz Alam, a Mumbai resident, was born and brought up in Aligarh, Uttar Pradesh. He has studied commerce from Aligarh Muslim University and done his masters in finance. He was a stock sub-broker and wealth manager before moved to Mumbai. He indulged in Urdu poetry and literature at a very young age, which influenced him to become a lyricist and writer. Afroz is passionate about history, mythology</span>
  <span id="freeText10195930897769430267" style="display:none">Afroz Alam, a Mumbai resident, was born and brought up in Aligarh, Uttar Pradesh. He has studied commerce from Aligarh Muslim University and done his masters in finance. He was a stock sub-broker and wealth manager before moved to Mumbai. He indulged in Urdu poetry and literature at a very young age, which influenced him to become a lyricist and writer. Afroz is passionate about history, mythology, and mysteries. Adhaata Asao’s Liege is his debut book. This book shows his interest in mythology and religions. </span>
